title: "8.10 keeps freezing"

### Post by Miroku on 2008-11-05
hello again, so i just recently installed 32bit ibex. everything was running fine untill i started up my computer 2 days ago. i noticed that it had not mounted the other partitions of my hdd, so when i loaded up amarok, it could not find my media partition. so i manually mounted it and had amarok rebuild. as it was doing this, ubuntu froze completely. mouse and all. keyboard was not responsive (i tried alt + sysrq + b which also did not work). i was forced to do a hard shut down. i restarted and then i remounted my partition before using amarok but then when i launched amarok, it froze again same like last time. now tonite, i did not open amarok, i just had mounted the partitions and when i tried to move a video file from the linux partition to my other partition, it froze again! its gettin me frustrated because i have no idea how to even diagnose the problem because there are no logs. please advise.

---

### Post by mapes12 on 2008-11-06
Could we have a look at how your machine is configured please. Post the output to: ```
sudo lshw
```

Also:

1. Was 8.10 a fresh installation or an upgrade?
2. Was your system working OK prior to the issues you have posted about?
3. If the answer to no.2 is yes what have you changed or added to the system since then e.g. any packages installed?

### Post by mocha on 2008-11-07
Usually hard lockups on linux are due to hardware problems.  You say that it locks when copying files?  Are you overclocking the CPU or FSB?  I had problems like this in the past when I was overclocking.  The interface to the disks just couldn't handle it.

If you are not overclocking then perhaps something is wrong with your disks.  Here are some helpful commands for testing disks.  Replace sda with your disk/partition names.  Use "fdisk -l" to see the names of your disks/partitions.

```
To get info on your partitions:

sudo hdparm -I /dev/sda > ~/sda_info

To run SMART tests on your hard drive, first install smartmontools, then:

sudo smartctl -t long /dev/sda

Then a few hours later run the following to see the final results:

sudo smartctl -l selftest /dev/sda

You can also look at the history of SMART errors being logged by the drive:

sudo smartctl -a /dev/sda

To check a drive for badblocks, boot with the live CD, don't mount the drive, find out which partition you want to scan using "sudo fdisk -l", then:

sudo badblocks -nvs /dev/sda

You can also do this, check the man page for more options:

sudo e2fsck -cfp /dev/sda1

The following will tell you if there are any blocks marked as bad on your partition:

sudo dumpe2fs -b /dev/sda1
```

---

### Post by tomthumb99 on 2009-01-29
Folks this thread helped greatly, my Maxtor disk are fine. It was found that have an AMD and Nvidia mobo chip set isssue with RAM above 1 Gig. It was hard to find, each time a large amount of disk I/O occures (ie: during sw installs), multiple files would be corrupted and bad inodes all over (ie fs: would go into ro mount).  Usually had to re-install OS after a week each time.

On the Grub bootup line, that PC was told only to use 1 Gig RAM.  It worlked, PC is now stable and can run 8.10 without  a  weekly re-install.  I also disable the disk write cache, kept MDA on.

---

### Post by tomthumb99 on 2009-10-27
Folks,

I solved mt prob by finding bad DIMM board.  I was having odd exe corruption,  if you see that run a memory check for 4 hours.  Had bad board, never thought those has issues, thought bios did test.   Now my OS does not get corrupted every third boot.
